‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§∏‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á- ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ (‡§ï‡§æ. ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•å. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•≠‡•¨) ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä’ ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§ø- “‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ 1 ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‚Äù ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‘‡§∏‡§≤‡•ã‡§Æ’ ‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç, ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He may set up the two fires 2 under the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs; for they, the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs, are doubtless Agni’s asterism, so that if he sets up his fires under Agni’s asterism, (he will bring about) a correspondence (between his fires and the asterism): for this reason he may set up his fires under the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs.

‡§Ö‡§•‡•à‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§è‡§ï‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡§É ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§è‡§ï-‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø-‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø-‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§É‚Äì‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø, ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∑‡§ü‡•ç‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‘‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§É’ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç 1 ‘‡§è‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‘‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á’ ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‘‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§ø’ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‘‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø’ ‡•§ ‘‡§§‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç, ‡§è‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‘‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç’ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•® ‡••

Eggeling
  1. Moreover, the other lunar asterisms (consist of) one, two, three or four (stars), so that the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs are the most numerous (of asterisms) 3: hence he thereby obtains an abundance. For this reason he may set up his fires under the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs.

Eggeling
  1. And again, they do not move away from the eastern quarter, whilst the other asterisms do move from the eastern quarter. Thus his (two fires) are established in the eastern quarter: for this reason he may set up his fires under the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs.

Eggeling
  1. On the other hand (it is argued) why he should not set up the fires under the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs. Originally, namely, the latter were the wives of the Bears (rÃ•ksha); for the seven RÃ•shis 7 were in former times

called the RÃ•kshas (bears). They were, however, precluded from intercourse (with their husbands), for the latter, the seven RÃ•shis, rise in the north, and they (the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs) in the east. Now it is a misfortune for one to be precluded from intercourse (with his wife): he should therefore not set up his fires under the KrÃ•ttikƒÅs, lest he should thereby be precluded from intercourse.

‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ß‡•Ä‡§§ ‡•§ ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ß‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§ ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§è‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Å‡§É, ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§µ‡•à‡§µ ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•à‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø- ‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•• ‡•¨ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ß‡•á’ ‡§Ü‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡•§ ‘‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§É’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ó‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£‡•à‡§ï‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§É ‘‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Å‡§É’ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‘‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É’ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§£‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø- ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡•¨ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He may also set up his fires under (the asterism of Rohi·πáƒ´. For under Rohi·πáƒ´ it was that PrajƒÅpati, when desirous of progeny (or creatures), set up his fires. He created beings, and the creatures produced by him remained invariable and constant 9, like (red) cows (rohi·πáƒ´): hence the cow-like nature of Rohi·πáƒ´. Rich in cattle and offspring therefore he becomes whosoever, knowing this, sets up his fires under Rohi·πáƒ´.

Eggeling
  1. Under Rohi·πáƒ´, indeed, the cattle set up their fires, thinking that they might attain to (ruh) the desire (or love) of men. They did attain to the

desire of men; and whatever desire the cattle then obtained in regard to men, that same desire he obtains, in regard to cattle, whosoever, knowing this, sets up his fire under Rohi·πáƒ´.

Eggeling
  1. He may also set up his fires under (the asterism of) MrÃ•ga≈õƒ´rsha. For MrÃ•ga≈õƒ´rsha, indeed, is the head of PrajƒÅpati 13; and the head (≈õiras) means excellence (≈õrƒ´), for the head does indeed mean excellence: hence they say of him who is the most excellent (≈õresh·π≠·∏•a) of a community, that he is the head of that community. Excellence therefore he attains whosoever, knowing this, sets up his fire under MrÃ•ga≈õƒ´rsha.

Eggeling
  1. On the other hand (it is argued) why one should not set up his fire under MrÃ•ga≈õƒ´rsha 16. The latter, indeed, is PrajƒÅpati’s body. Now, when they (the gods) on that occasion pierced him 17 with what is called ’the three-knotted arrow,’ he abandoned that

body, for the body is a mere relic (or dwelling, vƒÅstu), unholy and sapless. He should therefore not set up his fires under MrÃ•ga≈õƒ´rsha.

Eggeling
  1. But he may, nevertheless, set them up (under MrÃ•ga≈õƒ´rsha). For, assuredly, the body of that god, PrajƒÅpati, is neither a relic nor unholy, 20: he may therefore set up (his fires under MrÃ•ga≈õƒ´rsha). ‘Under the Punarvas≈´ he should perform the PunarƒÅdheya 21,’ thus (it is prescribed).

‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§Æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç 14 ‡•§ ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§™‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§è‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§π- ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø’ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø‡§É’ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•ã ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§É’ ‘‡§á‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ; ‡§Ö‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•å ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•å; “‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É‚Äù- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ó‡§£‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É’ ‡§è‡§µ ‘‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§É’, ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ ‘‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§Ü‡§π- ‡§ï‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§§‡§É ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ 22 ‡•§ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§É ‘‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§É’ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§â‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• ‡•ß‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He may also set up his fires under the Phalgunƒ´s. They, the Phalgunƒ´s, are Indra’s asterism 23, and even correspond to him in name; for indeed Indra is also called Arjuna, this being his mystic name; and they (the Phalgunƒ´s) are also called Arjunƒ´s. Hence he overtly calls them Phalgunƒ´s, for who dares to use his (the god’s) mystic name? Moreover, the sacrificer himself is Indra, so that he in that case sets up his fires under his own asterism. Indra is the deity of the sacrifice; and accordingly his AgnyƒÅdheya is thereby brought

into relation with Indra. He may set up the fires under the first (P≈´rva-phalgunƒ´s)–whereby an advancing (successful) sacrifice accrues to him; or he may set them up under the second (Uttara-phalgunƒ´s)–whereby a progressive (uttarƒÅvat) improvement accrues to him.

Eggeling
  1. Let him set up his fires under the asterism Hasta 25, whosoever should wish that (presents) should be offered him: then indeed (that will take place) forthwith; for whatever is offered with the hand (hasta), that indeed is given to him.

Eggeling
  1. He may also set up his fires under CitrƒÅ. Now the gods and the Asuras, both of them sprung from PrajƒÅpati, were contending for superiority. Both parties were desirous of rising to yonder world, the sky. The Asuras then constructed the fire (altar) called rauhi·πáa (fit to ascend by), thinking, ‘Thereby we shall ascend (ƒÅ-ruh) to the sky 28.’

Eggeling
  1. Indra then considered 29, ‘If they construct that (fire-altar), they will certainly prevail over us.’ He secured a brick and proceeded thither, passing himself off for a BrƒÅhman.

When he said, ‘I shall take back this (brick) which belongs to me.’ He took hold of it and pulled it out; and on its being pulled out, the fire-altar fell down; and along with the falling fire-altar the Asuras fell down. He then converted those bricks into thunderbolts and clove the (Asuras’) necks.

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon the gods assembled and said, ‘Wonderfully (citram) indeed it has fared with us who have slain so many enemies!’ Hence the wonderful nature (citrƒÅtva) 37 of the asterism

CitrƒÅ; and verily wonderfully it fares with him, and he slays his rivals, his spiteful enemy, whosoever, knowing this, sets up his fires under CitrƒÅ. A Kshatriya, therefore, should especially desire to take advantage of this asterism; since such a one is anxious to strike, to vanquish his enemies.

Eggeling
  1. Originally these (nakshatras) were so many different powers (kshatra), just as that sun yonder. But as soon as he rose, he took from them (ƒÅ-dƒÅ) their energy, their power; therefore he (the sun) is called ƒÄditya, because he took from them their energy, their power 38.

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò) ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§® ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§µ·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö·≥ò‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏·≥ò ‡§è‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•Å·≥ò‡§™‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§µ·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

‡§§‡•á·≥ò ‡§π ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§ä‡§ö‡•Å‡§É‡••
(‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò) ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§® ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§µ·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö·≥ò‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏·≥ò ‡§è‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•Å·≥ò‡§™‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§µ·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§§‡•á·≥ò ‡§π ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§ä‡§ö‡•Å‡§É‡••
‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§è‡§µ·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç 39 ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏·≥ò ‡§è‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•à‡§µ·≥ò ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•Å·≥ò‡§™‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§è‡§µ·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

‡§§‡•á ‡§π ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ä‡§ö‡•Å‡§É- ‘‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç, ‡§® ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç’ ‡§á‡§µ‡§ø‡§É ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç, ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§ ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§, ‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡•ß‡•Ø ‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡•á ‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§

‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø- ‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø’ ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‘‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø’ ‘‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç,’ ‘‡§Ü‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á’, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§∂‡§§‡§™‡§•‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• (‡•®-‡•ß-‡•®) ‡••

Eggeling
  1. The gods then said, ‘They who have been powers, shall no longer (na) be powers (kshatra) 44!’ Hence the powerlessness (na-kshatratvam) of the nakshatras. For this reason also one need only take the sun for one’s nakshatra (star), since he took away from them their energy, their power. But if he (the sacrificer) should nevertheless be desirous of having a nakshatra (under which to set up his fires), then assuredly that sun is a faultless nakshatra for him; and through that auspicious day (marked by the rising and setting of the sun) he should endeavour to obtain the benefits of whichever of those asterisms he might desire. Let him therefore take the sun alone for his nakshatra 45.

The KƒÅ·πáva text has: ‘Other nakshatras are (i.e. consist of) four; and there is here an abundance, so that he thereby obtains abundance.’ ↩︎

  13. 284:1 For the mythical allusions in this and the succeeding paragraphs, we have to compare ≈öat. Br. I, 7, 4, 1; Ait. Br. III, 33.   28. 286:2 In Taitt. Br. I, 1, 2, 4-6 this myth is related as follows: ‘There were Asuras, named KƒÅlaka√±jas. They constructed a fire (altar) with a view to (gaining) the world of heaven. They put, every man of them, a brick to it. Indra, passing himself off for a BrƒÅhman, put a brick on for himself, saying, “This one, Cƒ´tra (the wonderful or bright one) by name, is for me!” They climbed up to heaven; Indra, however, pulled out his brick, and they tumbled down. And they who tumbled down, became spiders: two of them flew up, and they became the two heavenly dogs.’ On this myth, Dr. A. Kuhn, ‘√úber entwickelungsstufen der mythenbildung,’ p. 129, remarks: ‘The myth given in Homer’s Od. xi, 305-325, of Otos and Ephialtes, who, in order to fight the immortal gods, piled Ossa on Olympos, and Pelion on Ossa, of ·ºµŒΩ·æΩ Œø·ΩêœÅŒ±ŒΩ·Ω∏œÇ, and who are destroyed by Apollon, shows an obvious resemblance to these Indian myths; the more so, if we divest the latter of their BrƒÅhmanical form, by which altar-bricks are substituted for mountains; and if we hear in mind that the later versions of the myth, e.g. in the well-known passage of Ovid, put the Gigantes in the place of the Aloades.’ See also Weber, Nakshatra, II, p. 372. ↩︎
